00001  ; Alicie, 2022, based on original work by "Keith".
00002  
00003      .OPT Proc65816
00004  
00005  ; Zero-page variables that are temporarily used when executing commands
00006  ; from the debugger. When the monitor is entered, their values are saved
00007  ; into the ZP save area in work RAM (RAM_ZP_SAVE), and restored before
00008  ; control is returned to the user's program, so their use by the debugger
00009  ; and monitor is transparent to the user.
00010    0000              DBG_VAR_00                  = $00
00011    0001              DBG_VAR_01                  = $01
00012    0002              DBG_VAR_02                  = $02
00013    0003              DBG_VAR_03                  = $03
00014    0004              DBG_VAR_04                  = $04
00015  
00016  ; Save-area in work-RAM for A.
00017    7E00              RAM_A_SAVE                  = $7E00
00018  
00019  ; Save-area in work-RAM for X.
00020    7E02              RAM_X_SAVE                  = $7E02
00021  
00022  ; Save-area in work-RAM for Y.
00023    7E04              RAM_Y_SAVE                  = $7E04
00024  
00025  ; Save-area in work-RAM for PC.
00026    7E06              RAM_PC_SAVE                 = $7E06
00027  
00028  ; Save-area in work-RAM for DP.
00029    7E08              RAM_DP_SAVE                 = $7E08
00030  
00031  ; Save-area in work-RAM for the stack pointer.
00032    7E0A              RAM_SP_SAVE                 = $7E0A
00033  
00034  ; Save-area in work-RAM for the P register.
00035    7E0C              RAM_P_SAVE                  = $7E0C
00036  
00037  ; Save-area in work-RAM for the emulation bit. This can be thought of
00038  ; as an extenstion bit to P. If E=1, the CPU is in emulation mode.
00039    7E0D              RAM_E_SAVE                  = $7E0D
00040  
00041  ; Save-area in work-RAM for the PB register.
00042    7E0E              RAM_PB_SAVE                 = $7E0E
00043  
00044  ; Save-area in work-RAM for the DB register.
00045    7E0F              RAM_DB_SAVE                 = $7E0F
00046  
00047  ; The auto-detected CPU type (0=65C02, 1=65816).
00048    7E10              RAM_CPU_TYPE                = $7E10
00049  
00050  ; 1 if the the monitor is currently being executed, 0 if user code.
00051    7E11              RAM_IN_MONITOR              = $7E11
00052  
00053  ; Why control has returned to the ROM monitor:
00054  ;    2: A BRK instruction was executed.
00055  ;    7: An NMI was generated.
00056    7E13              RAM_ENTER_MONITOR_REASON    = $7E13
00057  
00058  ; Five-byte area where $00-$04 are saved.
00059    7E14              RAM_ZP_SAVE                 = $7E14
00060  
00061  ; Flag variable at $7E19 of unknown use. It only ever gets set to 0.
00062    7E19              RAM_VAR_7E19                = $7E19
00063  
00064  ; Variable at $7E1A of unknown use. It gets set to 0, and apparently not used.
00065    7E1A              RAM_VAR_7E1A                = $7E1A
00066  
00067  ; Save-area in work-RAM for the system VIA's registers.
00068    7E1C              RAM_PCR_SAVE                = $7E1C
00069    7E1D              RAM_DDRB_SAVE               = $7E1D
00070    7E1E              RAM_DDRA_SAVE               = $7E1E
00071  
00072  ; Vectors in RAM which are called directly from the vectors in FLASH.
00073  ; These vectors are typically not overridden by the user, since they
00074  ; perform critical system and debugger operations.
00075    7E70              IRQ_02_ENTRY_VECTOR         = $7E70
00076    7E72              NMI_02_ENTRY_VECTOR         = $7E72
00077    7E74              BRK_816_ENTRY_VECTOR        = $7E74
00078    7E76              NMI_816_ENTRY_VECTOR        = $7E76
00079  
00080  ; The start of the shadow vectors. There are 14 in total. Not all are used.
00081    7EE4              SHADOW_VECTOR_START         = $7EE4
00082  
00083  ; Shadow vectors for 816 mode, which the user may set to hook the vector.
00084    7EE4              SHADOW_VEC_COP_816          = $7EE4
00085    7EE6              SHADOW_VEC_BRK_816          = $7EE6 ; unused?
00086    7EE8              SHADOW_VEC_ABORT_816        = $7EE8
00087    7EEA              SHADOW_VEC_NMI_816          = $7EEA ; unused?
00088    7EEC              SHADOW_VEC_RSVD_816         = $7EEC ; unused?
00089    7EEE              SHADOW_VEC_IRQ_816          = $7EEE
00090  
00091  ; Shadow vectors for the 65816 running in '02 emulation mode.
00092    7EF0              SHADOW_VEC_RSVD1_02         = $7EF0 ; unused
00093    7EF2              SHADOW_VEC_RSVD2_02         = $7EF2 ; unused
00094    7EF4              SHADOW_VEC_COP_02           = $7EF4
00095    7EF6              SHADOW_VEC_RSVD3_02         = $7EF6 ; unused
00096    7EF8              SHADOW_VEC_ABORT_02         = $7EF8
00097  
00098  ; Shadow vectors for all 65xx processors.
00099    7EFA              SHADOW_VEC_NMI_02           = $7EFA ; unused
00100    7EFC              SHADOW_VEC_RESET_02         = $7EFC ; unused
00101    7EFE              SHADOW_VEC_IRQ_02           = $7EFE
00102  
00103  ; IO for the VIA which is used for the USB debugger interface.
00104  ; Unused registers are commented-out.
00105    7FE0              SYSTEM_VIA_IOB              = $7FE0 ; Port B IO register
00106    7FE1              SYSTEM_VIA_IOA              = $7FE1 ; Port A IO register
00107    7FE2              SYSTEM_VIA_DDRB             = $7FE2 ; Port B data direction register
00108    7FE3              SYSTEM_VIA_DDRA             = $7FE3 ; Port A data direction register
00109  ;SYSTEM_VIA_T1C_L           = $7FE4 ; Timer 1 counter/latches, low-order
00110  ;SYSTEM_VIA_T1C_H           = $7FE5 ; Timer 1 high-order counter
00111  ;SYSTEM_VIA_T1L_L           = $7FE6 ; Timer 1 low-order latches
00112  ;SYSTEM_VIA_T1L_H           = $7FE7 ; Timer 1 high-order latches
00113  ;SYSTEM_VIA_T2C_L           = $7FE8 ; Timer 2 counter/latches, lower-order
00114  ;SYSTEM_VIA_T2C_H           = $7FE9 ; Timer 2 high-order counter
00115  ;SYSTEM_VIA_SR              = $7FEA ; Shift register
00116    7FEB              SYSTEM_VIA_ACR              = $7FEB ; Auxilliary control register
00117    7FEC              SYSTEM_VIA_PCR              = $7FEC ; Peripheral control register
00118  ;SYSTEM_VIA_IFR             = $7FED ; Interrupt flag register
00119  ;SYSTEM_VIA_IER             = $7FEE ; Interrupt enable register
00120  ;SYSTEM_VIA_ORA_IRA	        = $7FEF ; Port A IO register, but no handshake
00121  
00122          ; FLASH contents start here.
00123  008000                        .ORG $8000
00124  
00125  Monitor_Start:
00126          .byte   "WDC"
00127          .BYTE   $FF
00128  
00129  Signature_String:
00130          .byte   $82,"$",$01,$FF
00131  
00132  Monitor_Version_String:
00133          .byte   "WDC65c816SK WDCMON Version =  2"
00134          .byte   ".0.4.3Version Date = Wed Mar 26"
00135          .byte   " 2014  2:46", $00
00136  
00137          ; Unused data in the monitor version string area.
00138          .byte   $FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF
00139          .byte   $FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF
00140          .byte   $FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF
00141          .byte   $FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF
00142          .byte   $FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF
00143          .BYTE   $FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF
00144  
00145  008080                        .ORG $8080
00146  ; A table of important pointers. This is located at address $8080, and
00147  ; is 128 bytes long in total, but not all of it is used. Not sure if the
00148  ; debugger uses this table for any reason, but user applications could
00149  ; use it, for example, to read and write to the USB FIFO.
00150  Pointer_Table:
00151  
00152      ; Used entries in the pointer table.
00153          .WORD   Signature_String
00154          .WORD   Initialize_System
00155          .WORD   Is_VIA_USB_RX_Data_Avail
00156          .WORD   Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00157          .WORD   Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00158          .WORD   RAM_IN_MONITOR
00159          .WORD   Monitor_Version_String
00160          .WORD   IRQ_02_ENTRY_VECTOR
00161          .WORD   IRQ_02_Entry_Vector_Default
00162          .WORD   NMI_02_Entry_Vector_Default
00163          .WORD   BRK_816_Entry_Vector_Default
00164          .WORD   NMI_816_Entry_Vector_Default
00165  
00166          ; Unused entries in the pointer table.
00167          .WORD   $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF
00168          .WORD   $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF
00169          .WORD   $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF
00170          .WORD   $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF
00171          .WORD   $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF
00172          .WORD   $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF
00173          .WORD   $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF
00174          .WORD   $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF
00175          .WORD   $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF
00176          .WORD   $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF
00177          .WORD   $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF
00178          .WORD   $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF
00179          .WORD   $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF
00180  
00181  008100                        .ORG $8100
00182  
00183  ; Called directly from FLASH vector on IRQ in emulation mode. IRQ and BRK
00184  ; are shared in this mode, so jump to monitor code which checks for BRK.
00185  IRQ_02_entry:
00186  008100  6C 70 7E              jmp     (IRQ_02_ENTRY_VECTOR)
00187  008103  EA                    NOP
00188  
00189  ; Called directly from FLASH vector on NMI in emulation mode. Jump to monitor
00190  ; code to break into the debugger.
00191  NMI_02_entry:
00192  008104  6C 72 7E              jmp     (NMI_02_ENTRY_VECTOR)
00193  008107  EA                    NOP
00194  
00195  ; Called directly from FLASH vector on BRK in 816 mode. Jump to monitor
00196  ; code to break into the debugger.
00197  BRK_816_entry:
00198  008108  6C 74 7E              jmp     (BRK_816_ENTRY_VECTOR)
00199  00810B  EA                    NOP
00200  
00201  ; Called directly from FLASH vector on NMI in 816 mode. Jump to monitor
00202  ; code to break into the debugger.
00203  NMI_816_entry:
00204  00810C  6C 76 7E              jmp     (NMI_816_ENTRY_VECTOR)
00205  00810F  EA                    NOP
00206  
00207  ; Called directly from FLASH vector on COP in emulation mode. Call the
00208  ; user's handler through the shadow vector.
00209  COP_02_entry:
00210  008110  6C F4 7E              jmp     (SHADOW_VEC_COP_02)
00211  
00212  ; Called directly from FLASH vector on ABORT in emulation mode. Call the
00213  ; user's handler through the shadow vector.
00214  ABORT_02_entry:
00215  008113  6C F8 7E              jmp     (SHADOW_VEC_ABORT_02)
00216  
00217  ; Called directly from FLASH vector on IRQ in 816 mode.
00218  ; BRK and IRQ are separate in 816 mode, so no need to run any monitor code.
00219  ; Simply invoke the user's IRQ handler through the shadow vector.
00220  IRQ_816_entry:
00221  008116  6C EE 7E              jmp     (SHADOW_VEC_IRQ_816)
00222  
00223  ; Called directly from FLASH vector on ABORT in 816 mode.
00224  ABORT_816_entry:
00225  008119  6C E8 7E              jmp     (SHADOW_VEC_ABORT_816)
00226  
00227  ; Called directly from FLASH vector on COP in 816 mode.
00228  COP_816_entry:
00229  00811C  6C E4 7E              jmp     (SHADOW_VEC_COP_816)
00230  
00231  ; Does nothing forever. Called directly from several reserved vectors, and
00232  ; is also the default handler for all shadow vectors.
00233  Infinite_Loop:
00234  00811F  20 73 86              jsr     Do_Nothing_Subroutine_3
00235  008122  80 FB                 BRA     Infinite_Loop
00236  
00237  ; Does nothing forever. Called directly from a reserved vector.
00238  Infinite_Loop_2:
00239  008124  E2 20                 SEP     #$20    ; Set A to 8-bit.
00240  008126  20 73 86              jsr     Do_Nothing_Subroutine_3
00241  008129  80 F9                 BRA     Infinite_Loop_2
00242  
00243  ; Called directly from FLASH vector on RESET. Always executed in emulation mode.
00244  RESET_entry:
00245          ; Save the CPU context, init vectors, and switch into emulation mode.
00246  00812B  20 31 81              JSR     Initialize_Upon_Reset
00247  
00248          ; Save a copy of ZP memory, and sync up with the debugger.
00249  00812E  4C DB 81              jmp     Save_ZP_Sync_With_Debugger
00250  
00251  ; Called in emulation mode when the CPU is reset.
00252  Initialize_Upon_Reset:
00253          ; Push processor status on stack. The stack is not initialized yet,
00254          ; but Continue_System_Init expects P and A to be pushed on the stack,
00255          ; and we know the stack will be somewhere in page 1, so there will be
00256          ; RAM there to support it.
00257  008131  08                    PHP
00258  
00259          ; Set A to 8-bit mode. But why? We know we're in emulation mode here.
00260  008132  E2 20                 SEP	#$20
00261  
00262          ; Push A, load A with 1, and continue with initialization.
00263  008134  48                    pha
00264  008135  A9 01                 lda     #$01
00265  008137  80 04                 BRA     Continue_System_Init
00266  
00267  ; Called to initialize the system. The only place this is explicitly called
00268  ; is from Initialize_Upon_Reset, which is executed in emulation mode when the
00269  ; CPU is reset. But, there is a pointer to this function in the data pointer
00270  ; table, so perhaps the debugger calls it to reset the system. As such, this
00271  ; function ensures it works correctly even if called from native mode.
00272  Initialize_System:
00273          ; Push processor status on stack.
00274  008139  08                    PHP
00275  
00276          ; Set A to 8-bit mode and push it.
00277  00813A  E2 20                 SEP     #$20
00278  00813C  48                    PHA
00279  
00280  ; If called from an actual RESET, the CPU will be in emulation mode. If called
00281  ; through the data pointer table, the CPU may be in native mode with 8-bit A.
00282  ; Upon return, the CPU will be in emulation mode.
00283  Continue_System_Init:
00284  
00285          ; Disable interrupts and clear the decimal flag.
00286  00813D  78                    SEI
00287  00813E  D8                    CLD
00288  
00289          ; Zero a couple of variables whose use is currently unknown.
00290  00813F  9C 1A 7E              stz     RAM_VAR_7E1A
00291  008142  9C 19 7E              STZ     RAM_VAR_7E19
00292  
00293          ; Switch to native mode.
00294  008145  18                    clc
00295  008146  FB                    XCE
00296  
00297          ; Set XY to 16-bit mode and save them into the RAM save area.
00298  008147  C2 10                 REP     #$10
00299  008149  8E 02 7E              stx     RAM_X_SAVE
00300  00814C  8C 04 7E              STY     RAM_Y_SAVE
00301  
00302          ; Set A and XY to 8-bit mode.
00303  00814F  E2 30                 SEP     #$30
00304  
00305          ; Pull the prior value of A (8-bits) into X, and P into Y.
00306  008151  FA                    plx
00307  008152  7A                    PLY
00308  
00309          ; Save the processor status byte into the RAM save area.
00310  008153  8C 0C 7E              STY     RAM_P_SAVE
00311  
00312          ; Push 8-bit A back onto the stack.
00313  008156  48                    PHA
00314  
00315          ; Move the prior 8-bit value of A from X back into A.
00316  008157  8A                    TXA
00317  
00318          ; Set A to 16-bit mode.
00319  008158  C2 20                 REP     #$20
00320  
00321          ; Save A (all 16 bits) into the RAM save area.
00322  00815A  8F 00 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_A_SAVE
00323  
00324          ; Save DP (16 bits) into the RAM save area.
00325  00815E  7B                    TDC
00326  00815F  8F 08 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_DP_SAVE
00327  008163  3B                    TSC
00328  
00329          ; Save the 16-bit stack pointer into the RAM save area.
00330  008164  18                    CLC
00331  008165  69 03 00              ADC     \2#$03
00332  008168  8F 0A 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_SP_SAVE
00333  
00334          ; Set A and XY to 8-bit mode.
00335  00816C  E2 30                 SEP     #$30
00336  
00337          ; Save the 8-bit program bank into the RAM save area.
00338  00816E  4B                    PHK
00339  00816F  68                    pla
00340  008170  8F 0E 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_PB_SAVE
00341  
00342          ; Save the 8-bit data bank into the RAM save area.
00343  008174  8B                    PHB
00344  008175  68                    PLA
00345  008176  8F 0F 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_DB_SAVE
00346  
00347          ; Save the emulation mode flag into the RAM save area. Note it gets
00348          ; saved as "1", which means the CPU will be in emulation mode once
00349          ; the context is restored and the user's code is executed.
00350  00817A  A9 01                 lda     #$01
00351  00817C  8F 0D 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_E_SAVE
00352  
00353          ; CPU detection code. Determine if this CPU is a 65C02 or 65816.
00354  
00355          ; Try to switch into emulation mode.
00356  008180  38                    SEC
00357  008181  FB                    XCE     ; This is a NOP on a 65C02.
00358  
00359          ; Try to switch into native mode.
00360  008182  18                    CLC
00361  008183  FB                    XCE     ; This is a NOP on a 65C02. C will be set on a 65816.
00362  
00363          ; X = 0 if the CPU is a 65C02.
00364  008184  A2 00                 LDX     #$00
00365  
00366          ; If carry is clear, the CPU is 65C02, not 65816.
00367  008186  90 01                 BCC     .skip_inx
00368  
00369          ; If the CPU is a 65816, carry will be set, and X will be 1.
00370  008188  E8                    INX
00371  
00372  .skip_inx:
00373  008189  FB                    XCE     ; Switch into emulation mode. This is a NOP on a 65C02.
00374  00818A  8E 10 7E              STX     RAM_CPU_TYPE
00375  
00376          ; Pull the prior value of A, pushed before the call to
00377          ; Continue_System_Init. If this was called from a physical
00378          ; RESET, $01 is pushed. Otherwise, whatever was in A is pushed.
00379  00818D  68                    PLA
00380  00818E  F0 16                 BEQ     .skip_shadow_vec_init
00381  
00382          ; a RESET has occurred, so initialize all the shadow vectors.
00383          ; Initialize all shadow vectors to point to an infinite loop.
00384          ; Done in two passes. This pass sets the LSB of the vector.
00385  008190  A9 1F                 lda     #<Infinite_Loop
00386  008192  A2 1C                 ldx     #$1C
00387  .lsb_loop:
00388  008194  9D E2 7E              sta     SHADOW_VECTOR_START-2,x
00389  008197  CA                    dex
00390  008198  CA                    dex
00391  008199  D0 F9                 BNE     .lsb_loop
00392  
00393          ; Finish initializing the shadow registers by writing the MSB.
00394  00819B  A9 81                 lda     #>Infinite_Loop
00395  00819D  A2 1C                 ldx     #$1C
00396  .msb_loop:
00397  00819F  9D E3 7E              sta     SHADOW_VECTOR_START-1,x
00398  0081A2  CA                    dex
00399  0081A3  CA                    dex
00400  0081A4  D0 F9                 BNE     .msb_loop
00401  
00402  .skip_shadow_vec_init:
00403          ; We're now in the debugging monitor.
00404  0081A6  A9 01                 LDA     #$01
00405  0081A8  8D 11 7E              STA     RAM_IN_MONITOR
00406  
00407          ; Store 0 in the location after RAM_IN_MONITOR. Not sure why.
00408  0081AB  3A                    dec
00409  0081AC  8D 12 7E              STA     RAM_IN_MONITOR+1
00410  
00411          ; Set a pointer to the default BRK handler when in native mode.
00412  0081AF  A9 32                 lda     #<BRK_816_Entry_Vector_Default
00413  0081B1  8D 74 7E              sta     BRK_816_ENTRY_VECTOR
00414  0081B4  A9 85                 lda     #>BRK_816_Entry_Vector_Default
00415  0081B6  8D 75 7E              STA     BRK_816_ENTRY_VECTOR+1
00416          
00417          ; Set a pointer to the default NMI handler when in native mode.
00418  0081B9  A9 3F                 LDA     #<NMI_816_Entry_Vector_Default
00419  0081BB  8D 76 7E              STA     NMI_816_ENTRY_VECTOR
00420  0081BE  A9 85                 LDA     #>NMI_816_Entry_Vector_Default
00421  0081C0  8D 77 7E              STA     NMI_816_ENTRY_VECTOR+1
00422  
00423          ; Set a pointer to the default IRQ entry vector.
00424  0081C3  A9 AF                 lda     #<IRQ_02_Entry_Vector_Default
00425  0081C5  8D 70 7E              sta     IRQ_02_ENTRY_VECTOR
00426  0081C8  A9 84                 lda     #>IRQ_02_Entry_Vector_Default
00427  0081CA  8D 71 7E              STA     IRQ_02_ENTRY_VECTOR+1
00428  
00429          ; Set a pointer to the default NMI entry vector.
00430  0081CD  A9 CF                 lda     #<NMI_02_Entry_Vector_Default
00431  0081CF  8D 72 7E              sta     NMI_02_ENTRY_VECTOR
00432  0081D2  A9 84                 lda     #>NMI_02_Entry_Vector_Default
00433  0081D4  8D 73 7E              STA     NMI_02_ENTRY_VECTOR+1
00434  
00435  0081D7  20 B1 85              jsr     Initialize_System_VIA
00436  0081DA  60                    rts
00437  
00438  ; Saves the first 5 bytes of zero-page memory, and syncs with the debugger,
00439  ; allowing it to control the device.
00440  ; Upon entry, the CPU will always be in emulation mode.
00441  Save_ZP_Sync_With_Debugger:
00442          ; Copy the first 5 bytes of ZP to the work area in RAM.
00443  0081DB  A2 04                 ldx     #$04
00444  .copy_loop:
00445  0081DD  BD 00 00              lda     \2DBG_VAR_00,x
00446  0081E0  9D 14 7E              sta     RAM_ZP_SAVE,x
00447  0081E3  CA                    dex
00448  0081E4  10 F7                 BPL     .copy_loop
00449  
00450  .begin_debugger_sync:
00451          ; Read the first snc char from the debugger.
00452  0081E6  20 06 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00453  
00454  .check_for_0x55:
00455          ; If the first sync char is not $55, restart the sync process.
00456  0081E9  C9 55                 cmp     #$55
00457  0081EB  D0 F9                 BNE     .begin_debugger_sync
00458  
00459          ; Read the second cync char from the debugger.
00460  0081ED  20 06 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00461  
00462          ; If the second sync char is not $AA, check for %55.
00463  0081F0  C9 AA                 CMP     #$AA
00464  0081F2  D0 F5                 BNE     .check_for_0x55
00465          
00466          ; Send a $CC to the debugger.
00467  0081F4  A9 CC                 lda     #$CC
00468  0081F6  20 2B 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00469  
00470          ; Read the command byte from the debugger.
00471  0081F9  20 06 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00472  
00473          ; See if the command is within the supported range. If not,
00474          ; restart the debugger sync sequence.
00475  0081FC  38                    sec
00476  0081FD  E9 00                 sbc     #$00
00477  0081FF  C9 0A                 cmp     #$0A
00478  008201  B0 E3                 BCS     .begin_debugger_sync
00479  
00480          ; Set up a simulated function call to jump to the handler
00481          ; for the selected debugger command. Multiple the command
00482          ; by two since each function pointer is two bytes.
00483  008203  0A                    asl
00484  008204  AA                    TAX
00485  
00486          ; Push the address-1 to return to once the command is complete.
00487          ; We'll return to .begin_debugger_sync:.
00488  008205  A9 81                 lda     #>{.begin_debugger_sync-1}
00489  008207  48                    pha
00490  008208  A9 E5                 lda     #<{.begin_debugger_sync-1}
00491  00820A  48                    PHA
00492  
00493          ; Push the jump table address and issue the RTS to call the handler.
00494  00820B  BD 15 82              lda     Cmd_Jump_Table+1,x
00495  00820E  48                    pha
00496  00820F  BD 14 82              lda     Cmd_Jump_Table,x
00497  008212  48                    pha
00498  008213  60                    rts
00499  
00500  ; Jump table for debugger commands.
00501  Cmd_Jump_Table:
00502          .WORD   Dbg_Cmd_0_Send_Zero         - 1
00503          .WORD   Dbg_Cmd_1_Seq_Test          - 1
00504          .WORD   Dbg_Cmd_2_Write_Mem         - 1
00505          .WORD   Dbg_Cmd_3_Read_Mem          - 1
00506          .WORD   Dbg_Cmd_4_Sys_Info          - 1
00507          .WORD   Dbg_Cmd_5_Exec              - 1
00508          .WORD   Dbg_Cmd_6_No_Op             - 1
00509          .WORD   Dbg_Cmd_7_No_Op             - 1
00510          .WORD   Dbg_Cmd_8_BRK               - 1
00511          .WORD   Dbg_Cmd_9_Read_Byte_and_BRK - 1
00512  
00513  ; Debugger command 0. Simply sends $00 to the debugger.
00514  Dbg_Cmd_0_Send_Zero:
00515  008228  A9 00                 LDA     #$00
00516  00822A  4C 2B 86              jmp     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00517  
00518  ; Debugger command 1: some kind of sequence test. Debugger sends a 16-bit
00519  ; count of the bytes to test. The debugger must then send an incrementing
00520  ; sequence of bytes, starting at $00 to the monitor. The monitor sends
00521  ; back the next expected byte. If the monitor receives a byte it does not
00522  ; expect, it enters an infinite loop.
00523  Dbg_Cmd_1_Seq_Test:
00524  
00525          ; DBG_VAR_02 is the next value in the sequence. Start with $00.
00526  00822D  A9 00                 lda     #$00
00527  00822F  8D 02 00              STA     \2DBG_VAR_02
00528  
00529         ; Read the LSB of the byte count.
00530  008232  20 06 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00531  008235  8D 00 00              sta     \2DBG_VAR_00
00532  
00533          ; Read the MSB of the byte count.
00534  008238  20 06 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00535  00823B  8D 01 00              STA     \2DBG_VAR_01
00536  
00537          ; If the byte count is 0, we're done.
00538  00823E  0D 00 00              ora     \2DBG_VAR_00
00539  008241  F0 26                 BEQ     .done
00540  
00541          ; Set up the count's MSB to be 1-based.
00542  008243  AD 00 00              LDA     \2DBG_VAR_00
00543  008246  F0 03                 beq     .read_next_byte
00544  008248  EE 01 00              INC     \2DBG_VAR_01
00545  
00546  .read_next_byte:
00547          ; Read the next byte in the sequence from the debugger.
00548  00824B  20 06 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00549  
00550          ; See if the received byte matches the next one in the sequence.
00551  00824E  CD 02 00              CMP     \2DBG_VAR_02
00552  008251  F0 05                 BEQ     .continue
00553  
00554          ; If the sequence is not correct, enter an infinite loop.
00555  .infinite_loop:
00556  008253  20 72 86              jsr     Do_Nothing_Subroutine_2
00557  008256  80 FB                 BRA     .infinite_loop
00558          
00559  .continue:
00560          ; Send the next byte in the sequence to the debugger.
00561  008258  1A                    inc
00562  008259  20 2B 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00563  
00564          ; Save the next byte in the sequence.
00565  00825C  EE 02 00              INC     \2DBG_VAR_02
00566  
00567          ; Decrement the byte count.
00568  00825F  CE 00 00              dec     \2DBG_VAR_00
00569  008262  D0 E7                 bne     .read_next_byte
00570  008264  CE 01 00              dec     \2DBG_VAR_01
00571  008267  D0 E2                 BNE     .read_next_byte
00572  
00573          ; All done with the command.
00574  008269  60            .done:  rts
00575  
00576  ; Debugger command 2: write memory. The debugger sends a 24-bit starting
00577  ; address, then a 16-bit count, and then the data to write. Memory writes
00578  ; to the first 5 bytes of memory are automatically redirected to the save
00579  ; area in work-RAM for these memory locations.
00580  Dbg_Cmd_2_Write_Mem:
00581  
00582          ; Read the 24-bit starting address, LSB-first.
00583  00826A  20 06 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00584  00826D  8D 00 00              sta     \2DBG_VAR_00	; 16-bit addr LSB
00585  008270  20 06 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00586  008273  8D 01 00              sta     \2DBG_VAR_01	; 16-bit addr MSB
00587  008276  20 06 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00588  008279  8D 02 00              STA     \2DBG_VAR_02	; bank
00589  
00590          ; Branch if bank is > $00.
00591  00827C  A9 00                 lda     #$00
00592  00827E  CD 02 00              cmp     \2DBG_VAR_02
00593  008281  90 1C                 BCC     .read_byte_count
00594  
00595          ; At this point, bank is $00. Branch if page (16-bit MSB) is > $80.
00596  008283  A9 80                 lda     #$80
00597  008285  CD 01 00              cmp     \2DBG_VAR_01
00598  008288  90 15                 BCC     .read_byte_count
00599  
00600          ; At this point, bank=0, page <= $80. Branch if addr LSB > $00.
00601  00828A  A9 00                 lda     #$00
00602  00828C  CD 00 00              cmp     \2DBG_VAR_00
00603  00828F  90 0E                 BCC     .read_byte_count
00604  
00605          ; At this point, bank=0, page <= $80, addr_LSB=0, which is the
00606          ; first byte of any page in RAM, plus the first page of FLASH,
00607          ; in bank 0. Now branch if bank <= 1, which is always the case,
00608          ; since bank is $00 at this point. Why are they doing all this?
00609  008291  A9 01                 lda     #$01
00610  008293  CD 02 00              cmp     \2DBG_VAR_02
00611  008296  B0 07                 BCS     .read_byte_count
00612  
00613          ; This code stores $01 in RAM_VAR_7E19, but this code is apparently
00614          ; never executed. This means RAM_VAR_7E19 will always be $00.
00615  008298  A9 01                 lda     #$01
00616  00829A  8D 19 7E              sta     RAM_VAR_7E19
00617  00829D  80 43                 BRA     .next_addr
00618  
00619  .read_byte_count:
00620          ; Read the 16-bit byte count from the debugger, LSB-first.
00621  00829F  20 06 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00622  0082A2  8D 03 00              sta     \2DBG_VAR_03
00623  0082A5  20 06 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00624  0082A8  8D 04 00              STA     \2DBG_VAR_04
00625  
00626          ; If the tranfer count is 0, cleanup and return.
00627  0082AB  0D 03 00              ora     \2DBG_VAR_03
00628  0082AE  F0 49                 BEQ     .cleanup
00629  
00630          ; Set the MSB of the transfer count to be 1-based.
00631  0082B0  A0 00                 ldy     #$00
00632  0082B2  AD 03 00              lda     \2DBG_VAR_03
00633  0082B5  F0 03                 beq     .transfer_byte
00634  0082B7  EE 04 00              INC     \2DBG_VAR_04
00635  
00636  .transfer_byte:
00637          ; If the address is not in the first bank and first page, then
00638          ; transfer the memory contents from the actual memory location.
00639  0082BA  AD 01 00              lda     \2DBG_VAR_01
00640  0082BD  0D 02 00              ora     \2DBG_VAR_02
00641  0082C0  D0 12                 BNE     .transfer_byte_from_real_addr
00642  
00643          ; Now see if the address is within the first five bytes of RAM.
00644          ; This address is used for debugger command parameters.
00645  0082C2  AD 00 00              lda     \2DBG_VAR_00
00646  0082C5  C9 05                 cmp     #$05
00647  0082C7  B0 0B                 BCS     .transfer_byte_from_real_addr
00648  
00649          ; The address is within the 5-byte debugger area in the zero-
00650          ; page. First, read the byte from the debugger to write.
00651  0082C9  A8                    tay
00652  0082CA  20 06 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00653  
00654          ; Now save the byte into the save area in work-RAM.
00655  0082CD  99 14 7E              STA     RAM_ZP_SAVE,y
00656  
00657          ; Move to the next byte to transfer.
00658  0082D0  A0 00                 ldy     #$00
00659  0082D2  F0 0E                 BEQ     .next_addr
00660  
00661  .transfer_byte_from_real_addr:
00662          ; Read the byte to write from the debugger.
00663  0082D4  20 06 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00664  
00665          ; See if we're running on a 65C02 or a 65816.
00666  0082D7  AE 10 7E              ldx     RAM_CPU_TYPE
00667  0082DA  D0 04                 BNE     .cpu_is_65816
00668  
00669          ; For the 65C02, ignore the bank, and only use the 16-bit addr.
00670  0082DC  91 00                 sta     (DBG_VAR_00),y
00671  0082DE  F0 02                 BEQ     .next_addr
00672  
00673  .cpu_is_65816:
00674          ; Use the ZP-indirect-long mode to write to the full 24-bit addr.
00675  0082E0  87 00                 STA     [0]
00676  
00677  .next_addr:
00678          ; Move to the next address.
00679  0082E2  EE 00 00              INC     \2DBG_VAR_00
00680  0082E5  D0 08                 bne     .dec_count
00681  0082E7  EE 01 00              inc     \2DBG_VAR_01
00682  0082EA  D0 03                 bne     .dec_count
00683  0082EC  EE 02 00              INC     \2DBG_VAR_02
00684  
00685  .dec_count:
00686          ; Decrement the transfer count, and see if we're done.
00687  0082EF  CE 03 00              DEC     \2DBG_VAR_03
00688  0082F2  D0 C6                 bne     .transfer_byte
00689  0082F4  CE 04 00              dec     \2DBG_VAR_04
00690  0082F7  D0 C1                 BNE     .transfer_byte
00691  
00692  .cleanup:
00693          ; Clear RAM_VAR_7E19 for some unknown reason. But it would never
00694          ; get set in the first place, so this code seems unnecessary.
00695  0082F9  AD 19 7E              LDA     RAM_VAR_7E19
00696  0082FC  F0 03                 beq     .done
00697  0082FE  9C 19 7E              STZ     RAM_VAR_7E19
00698  
00699  008301  60            .done:  rts
00700  
00701  ; Debugger command 3: read memory. The debugger sends a 24-bit starting
00702  ; address, then a 16-bit count. and then the monitor sends the request
00703  ; memory contents to the debugger. Memory reads to the first 5 bytes of
00704  ; memory are automatically redirected to the save area in work-RAM for
00705  ; these memory locations.
00706  Dbg_Cmd_3_Read_Mem:
00707          ; Read the 24-bit starting address, LSB-first.
00708  008302  20 06 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00709  008305  8D 00 00              sta     \2DBG_VAR_00	; 16-bit LSB
00710  008308  20 06 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00711  00830B  8D 01 00              sta     \2DBG_VAR_01	; Page
00712  00830E  20 06 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00713  008311  8D 02 00              STA     \2DBG_VAR_02	; Bank
00714  
00715          ; Read the 16-bit byte count, LSB-first.
00716  008314  20 06 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00717  008317  8D 03 00              sta     \2DBG_VAR_03	; Count LSB
00718  00831A  20 06 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00719  00831D  8D 04 00              STA     \2DBG_VAR_04	; Count MSB
00720  
00721          ; If the byte count is 0, then we're done.
00722  008320  0D 03 00              ora     \2DBG_VAR_03
00723  008323  F0 46                 BEQ     .done
00724  
00725          ; Set up the count MSB to be 1-based.
00726  008325  A0 00                 ldy     #$00
00727  008327  AD 03 00              lda     \2DBG_VAR_03
00728  00832A  F0 03                 beq     .transfer_byte
00729  00832C  EE 04 00              INC     \2DBG_VAR_04
00730  
00731  .transfer_byte:
00732          ; If the address is not in the first bank and first page, then
00733          ; transfer the memory contents from the actual memory location.
00734  00832F  AD 01 00              lda     \2DBG_VAR_01
00735  008332  0D 02 00              ora     \2DBG_VAR_02
00736  008335  D0 0F                 BNE     .transfer_byte_from_real_addr
00737  
00738          ; Now see if the address is within the first five bytes of RAM.
00739          ; This address is used for debugger command parameters.
00740  008337  AD 00 00              lda     \2DBG_VAR_00
00741  00833A  C9 05                 cmp     #$05
00742  00833C  B0 08                 BCS     .transfer_byte_from_real_addr
00743  
00744          ; The address is within the 5-byte debugger area in the zero-page,
00745          ; so send the contents of the save area in RAM to the debugger.
00746  00833E  A8                    tay
00747  00833F  B9 14 7E              LDA     RAM_ZP_SAVE,y
00748  
00749          ; Move to the next byte to transfer.
00750  008342  A0 00                 ldy     #$00
00751  008344  F0 0B                 BEQ     .next_addr
00752  
00753  .transfer_byte_from_real_addr:
00754          ; See if we're running on a 65C02 or a 65816.
00755  008346  AD 10 7E              lda     RAM_CPU_TYPE
00756  008349  D0 04                 BNE     .cpu_is_65816
00757  
00758          ; For the 65C02, ignore the bank, and only use the 16-bit addr.
00759  00834B  B1 00                 lda     (DBG_VAR_00),y
00760  00834D  80 02                 BRA     .next_addr
00761  
00762  .cpu_is_65816:
00763          ; Use the ZP-indirect-long mode to read from the full 24-bit addr.
00764  00834F  A7 00                 LDA     [0]
00765  
00766  .next_addr:
00767          ; Send the byte read from memory to the debugger.
00768  008351  20 2B 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00769  
00770          ; Move to the next address.
00771  008354  EE 00 00              inc     \2DBG_VAR_00
00772  008357  D0 08                 bne     .dec_count
00773  008359  EE 01 00              inc     \2DBG_VAR_01
00774  00835C  D0 03                 bne     .dec_count
00775  00835E  EE 02 00              INC     \2DBG_VAR_02
00776  
00777  .dec_count:
00778          ; Decrement the transfer count, and see if we're done.
00779  008361  CE 03 00              DEC     \2DBG_VAR_03
00780  008364  D0 C9                 bne     .transfer_byte
00781  008366  CE 04 00              dec     \2DBG_VAR_04
00782  008369  D0 C4                 BNE     .transfer_byte
00783  
00784  00836B  60            .done:  rts
00785  
00786  ; Debugger command 4. Get System Info.
00787  Dbg_Cmd_4_Sys_Info:
00788          ; Send $00:7E00 to the debugger, which is the start of the monitor
00789          ; work-RAM. This same address is also sent later, for some reason.
00790  00836C  A9 00                 lda     #$00
00791  00836E  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00792  008371  A9 7E                 lda     #$7E
00793  008373  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00794  008376  A9 00                 lda     #$00
00795  008378  20 2B 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00796  
00797          ; Auto-detected CPU type.
00798  00837B  AD 10 7E              lda     RAM_CPU_TYPE
00799  00837E  20 2B 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00800  
00801          ; Board ID.
00802  008381  A9 58                 lda     #$58
00803  008383  20 2B 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00804  
00805          ; Send $00:7E00 to the debugger again.
00806  008386  A9 00                 lda     #$00
00807  008388  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00808  00838B  A9 7E                 lda     #$7E
00809  00838D  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00810  008390  A9 00                 LDA     #$00
00811  008392  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00812  
00813          ; Send the monitor ROM address ($00:8000).
00814  008395  A9 00                 lda     #$00
00815  008397  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00816  00839A  A9 80                 lda     #$80
00817  00839C  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00818  00839F  A9 00                 lda     #$00
00819  0083A1  20 2B 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00820  
00821          ; Shadow vector start (24-bit address, LSB-first).
00822  0083A4  A9 E4                 lda     #<SHADOW_VECTOR_START
00823  0083A6  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00824  0083A9  A9 7E                 LDA     #>SHADOW_VECTOR_START
00825  0083AB  20 2B 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00826  0083AE  A9 00                 lda     #$00
00827  0083B0  20 2B 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00828  
00829          ; Send the hardware base IO address ($00:7F00).
00830  0083B3  A9 00                 lda     #$00
00831  0083B5  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00832  0083B8  A9 7F                 lda     #$7F
00833  0083BA  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00834  0083BD  A9 00                 LDA     #$00
00835  0083BF  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00836  
00837          ; Send the hardware vector address ($00:FFE4).
00838  0083C2  A9 E4                 lda     #$E4
00839  0083C4  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00840  0083C7  A9 FF                 lda     #$FF
00841  0083C9  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00842  0083CC  A9 00                 LDA     #$00
00843  0083CE  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00844  
00845          ; Send the hardware base IO address ($00:7F00) again.
00846  0083D1  A9 00                 lda     #$00
00847  0083D3  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00848  0083D6  A9 7F                 lda     #$7F
00849  0083D8  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00850  0083DB  A9 00                 LDA     #$00
00851  0083DD  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00852  
00853          ; Send $00:7FFF. Not sure what this is, but it's the last byte of RAM.
00854  0083E0  A9 FF                 lda     #$FF
00855  0083E2  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00856  0083E5  A9 7F                 lda     #$7F
00857  0083E7  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00858  0083EA  A9 00                 LDA     #$00
00859  0083EC  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00860  
00861          ; Send $FF:FFFF. Not sure what it's used for.
00862  0083EF  A9 FF                 lda     #$FF
00863  0083F1  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00864  0083F4  A9 FF                 lda     #$FF
00865  0083F6  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00866  0083F9  A9 FF                 lda     #$FF
00867  0083FB  4C 2B 86              jmp     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00868  
00869  ; Debugger command 5. Restore the CPU context and execute from the saved context.
00870  Dbg_Cmd_5_Exec:
00871  
00872          ; Restore the user's state of the VIA's PCR register.
00873  0083FE  20 6B 86              JSR     Restore_VIA_PCR_State
00874  
00875          ; Restore the 5 zero-page variables from the copies in work-RAM.
00876  008401  A2 04                 LDX     #$04
00877  .copy_zp_var:
00878  008403  BD 14 7E              lda     RAM_ZP_SAVE,x
00879  008406  9D 00 00              sta     \2DBG_VAR_00,x
00880  008409  CA                    dex
00881  00840A  10 F7                 BPL     .copy_zp_var
00882  
00883          ; See if the CPU was running in emulation mode.
00884  00840C  AD 0D 7E              lda     RAM_E_SAVE
00885  00840F  F0 2D                 BEQ     .was_in_native_mode
00886  
00887          ; The CPU was in emulation mode. Restore the CPU context. Start off
00888          ; by restoring the stack and the index registers.
00889  008411  AE 0A 7E              ldx     RAM_SP_SAVE
00890  008414  9A                    txs
00891  008415  AE 02 7E              ldx     RAM_X_SAVE
00892  008418  AC 04 7E              LDY     RAM_Y_SAVE
00893  
00894          ; See what CPU type we're running.
00895  00841B  AD 10 7E              lda     RAM_CPU_TYPE
00896  00841E  D0 09                 BNE     .cpu_is_65816
00897  
00898          ; CPU is 65C02. The below code pushes the saved direct-page contents
00899          ; onto the stack. Not sure why, since in emulation mode, these will
00900          ; always both be 0.
00901  008420  AD 09 7E              lda     RAM_DP_SAVE+1
00902  008423  48                    pha
00903  008424  AD 08 7E              lda     RAM_DP_SAVE
00904  008427  48                    PHA
00905  
00906          ; Pull the direct-page register from the stack. But, since this is
00907          ; running on a 65C02, this will actually be a no-op. Seems like the
00908          ; stack will have two extra bytes on it (the direct page). Why?!?
00909  008428  2B                    PLD
00910  
00911  .cpu_is_65816:
00912          ; Set up a simulated ISR on the stack.
00913  008429  AD 07 7E              LDA     RAM_PC_SAVE+1
00914  00842C  48                    pha
00915  00842D  AD 06 7E              lda     RAM_PC_SAVE
00916  008430  48                    pha
00917  008431  AD 0C 7E              lda     RAM_P_SAVE
00918  008434  48                    PHA
00919  
00920          ; We're no longer in the ROM monitor since we're going to execute user code.
00921  008435  A9 00                 lda     #$00
00922  008437  8D 11 7E              STA     RAM_IN_MONITOR
00923  
00924          ; Restore the A register.
00925  00843A  AD 00 7E              LDA     RAM_A_SAVE
00926  
00927          ; Perform an RTI, restoring the CPU context as it was.
00928  00843D  40                    rti
00929  
00930  .was_in_native_mode:
00931          ; Set the CPU to native mode.
00932  00843E  18                    CLC
00933  00843F  FB                    XCE
00934  
00935          ; Set XY to 16-bit mode, and A to 8-bit mode.
00936  008440  E2 20                 SEP     #$20
00937  008442  C2 10                 REP     #$10
00938  
00939          ; Restore the 16-bit stack and Direct Page registers.
00940  008444  AE 0A 7E              ldx     RAM_SP_SAVE
00941  008447  9A                    txs
00942  008448  AE 08 7E              ldx     RAM_DP_SAVE
00943  00844B  DA                    phx
00944  00844C  2B                    PLD
00945  
00946          ; Set up a simulated ISR on the stack.
00947  00844D  AD 0E 7E              lda     RAM_PB_SAVE
00948  008450  48                    pha
00949  008451  AE 06 7E              ldx     RAM_PC_SAVE
00950  008454  DA                    phx
00951  008455  AD 0C 7E              lda     RAM_P_SAVE
00952  008458  48                    pha
00953  008459  AE 02 7E              ldx     RAM_X_SAVE
00954  00845C  AC 04 7E              LDY     RAM_Y_SAVE
00955  
00956          ; We're no longer in the ROM monitor since we're going to execute user code.
00957  00845F  A9 00                 lda     #$00
00958  008461  8D 11 7E              STA     RAM_IN_MONITOR
00959  
00960          ; Restore the data bank register.
00961  008464  AD 0F 7E              lda     RAM_DB_SAVE
00962  008467  48                    pha
00963  008468  AB                    PLB
00964  
00965          ; Set A to 16-bit mode.
00966  008469  C2 20                 REP     #$20
00967  
00968          ; Restore the 16-bit A register.
00969  00846B  AF 00 7E 00           LDA     \3RAM_A_SAVE
00970  
00971          ; Perform an RTI, restoring the CPU context as it was.
00972  00846F  40                    RTI
00973  
00974  ; Debugger commands 6 and 7. They do nothing.
00975  Dbg_Cmd_6_No_Op:
00976  Dbg_Cmd_7_No_Op:
00977  
00978          ; Return, making this debug command a no-op.
00979  008470  60                    rts
00980  
00981          ; This code is apparently never called.
00982  008471  4C 2B 86              jmp     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00983  008474  A9 25                 lda     #$25
00984  008476  80 20                 bra     Dbg_Cmd_8_Done
00985  008478  2B                    PLD
00986  008479  86 A9                 stx     $A9
00987  00847B  80 00                 bra     .branch
00988  .branch:
00989  00847D  20 2B 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00990          ; See notes for Dbg_Cmd_8_BRK about 8-bit LDA and BRK vs. 16-bit LDA.
00991  008480  A9 00                 LDA     #$00
00992          .DB     $00 ; Single-byte BRK instruction.
00993  008483  4C 2B 86              jmp     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00994  
00995  ; Debugger command 8. Executes a BRK instruction, causing the monitor to send
00996  ; a $02 to the debugger, as it normally does when a BRK is executed. Not sure why
00997  ; this debugger command exists, or how/if it is useful at all.
00998  Dbg_Cmd_8_BRK:
00999  008486  20 97 84              jsr     .clear_carry
01000  008489  90 06                 BCC     .on_carry_clear
01001  
01002          ; The following code is apparently never executed. See notes below
01003          ; regarding an 8-bit immediate LDA and BRK vs. a 16-bit immediate LDA.
01004  00848B  A9 01                 LDA     #$01
01005          .DB     $00 ; Single-byte BRK instruction.
01006  00848E  4C 2B 86              jmp     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
01007  
01008  .on_carry_clear:
01009  
01010          ; Perform an 8-bit immediate load, and generate a BRK. The BRK in this
01011          ; case is only a single byte, instead of two bytes which is typical.
01012          ; This could also be interpreted as a 16-bit immediate load of $0000,
01013          ; but since the CPU is always in emulation mode when this code is
01014          ; executed, it is clearer to write it as an 8-bit load and a BRK.
01015  008491  A9 00                 LDA     #$00
01016          .DB     $00 ; Single-byte BRK instruction.
01017  
01018          ; This is not executed because of the BRK above.
01019  008494  4C 2B 86              jmp     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
01020  
01021  .clear_carry:
01022  008497  18                    CLC
01023  
01024  Dbg_Cmd_8_Done:
01025  008498  60                    RTS
01026  
01027  ; Debugger command 9. Reads a byte from the debugger, and then executes a BRK
01028  ; instruction, which then sends a $02 to the debugger. Not sure why this
01029  ;debugger command exists, or how/if it is useful at all.
01030  Dbg_Cmd_9_Read_Byte_and_BRK:
01031          ; Read a data byte from the debugger.
01032  008499  20 06 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
01033  
01034  00849C  20 AD 84              jsr     .clear_carry
01035  00849F  90 06                 BCC     .on_carry_clear
01036  
01037          ; The following code is apparently never executed. See DBG_CMD_8_BRK
01038          ; regarding an 8-bit immediate LDA and BRK vs. a 16-bit immediate LDA.
01039  0084A1  A9 01                 LDA     #$01
01040          .DB     $00 ; Single-byte BRK instruction.
01041  0084A4  4C 2B 86              jmp     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
01042  
01043  .on_carry_clear:
01044          ; The following code is apparently never executed. See DBG_CMD_8_BRK
01045          ; regarding an 8-bit immediate LDA and BRK vs. a 16-bit immediate LDA.
01046  0084A7  A9 00                 LDA     #$00
01047          .DB     $00
01048  
01049          ; This is not executed because of the BRK above.
01050  0084AA  4C 2B 86              jmp     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
01051  
01052  .clear_carry:
01053  0084AD  18                    CLC
01054  0084AE  60                    rts
01055  
01056  ; The default handler for IRQ when in '02 emulation mode.
01057  ; At this point, we are in emulation mode, so A and XY are in 8-bit mode.
01058  IRQ_02_Entry_Vector_Default:
01059  0084AF  48                    PHA     ; Save the LSB of A on the stack.
01060  
01061          ; We're now executing the ROM monitor code.
01062  0084B0  A9 01                 lda     #$01
01063  0084B2  8F 11 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_IN_MONITOR
01064  0084B6  DA                    PHX     ; Save X on the stack.
01065  
01066          ; Get the pushed P (status reg). This includes the B flag which
01067          ; was pushed. We're in '02 mode, so we know the stack is at $100.
01068  0084B7  BA                    tsx
01069  0084B8  BD 03 01              lda     $103,x
01070  0084BB  FA                    PLX
01071  
01072          ; See if the pushed copy of B is set, indicating a BRK vs IRQ.
01073  0084BC  29 10                 and     #$10
01074  0084BE  D0 0A                 BNE     .on_BRK
01075  
01076          ; An IRQ was received. Clean up the stack and call the user's
01077          ; IRQ vector through the shadow vector at $7EFE.
01078  0084C0  A9 00                 lda     #$00
01079  0084C2  8F 11 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_IN_MONITOR	; No longer in ROM monitor code.
01080  
01081  0084C6  68                    pla
01082  0084C7  6C FE 7E              jmp     (SHADOW_VEC_IRQ_02)
01083  
01084  ; Called when a BRK instruction is executed.
01085  .on_BRK:
01086          ; Set RAM_ENTER_MONITOR_REASON to 2, indicating a BRK was executed.
01087  0084CA  A9 02                 LDA     #$02
01088  0084CC  4C E2 84              jmp     Save_Context_Enter_Monitor_02_Mode
01089  
01090  ; The default handler for NMI when in '02 emulation mode.
01091  NMI_02_Entry_Vector_Default:
01092  0084CF  48                    PHA     ; Save the LSB of A on the stack.
01093  
01094          ; See if we were running monitor code or user code.
01095  0084D0  AF 11 7E 00           LDA     \3RAM_IN_MONITOR
01096  0084D4  D0 0A                 BNE     .was_running_monitor_code
01097  
01098          ; We were running user code, but now we're in the monitor.
01099  0084D6  A9 01                 lda     #$01
01100  0084D8  8F 11 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_IN_MONITOR
01101  
01102          ; Set RAM_ENTER_MONITOR_REASON to 7, indicating an NMI was generated.
01103  0084DC  A9 07                 lda     #$07
01104  0084DE  80 02                 BRA     Save_Context_Enter_Monitor_02_Mode
01105          
01106  .was_running_monitor_code:
01107          ; An NMI ocurred while running the monitor code. Ignore it by
01108          ; restoring the context and returning from the interrupt.
01109  0084E0  68                    pla
01110  0084E1  40                    rti
01111  
01112  ; Called while in '02 emulation mode to save the CPU context and
01113  ; then enter the ROM monitor.
01114  ;
01115  ; On entry, A must contain the reason the monitor will be entered.
01116  Save_Context_Enter_Monitor_02_Mode:
01117  
01118          ; Enter native mode.
01119  0084E2  80 3D                 BRA     .enter_native_mode
01120  
01121          ; The above is not a subroutine call, so it does not return.
01122          ; I don't think the following code is ever executed. Instead,
01123          ; the BRA above switches the CPU into native mode, and then
01124          ; the native-mode routine is called to save the CPU context.
01125  
01126          ; Save the reason we're entering the monitor into work-RAM.
01127  0084E4  8D 13 7E              STA     RAM_ENTER_MONITOR_REASON
01128  
01129          ; Save the 8-bit CPU context into work-RAM.
01130  0084E7  68                    pla
01131  0084E8  8D 00 7E              sta     RAM_A_SAVE
01132  0084EB  8E 02 7E              stx     RAM_X_SAVE
01133  0084EE  8C 04 7E              sty     RAM_Y_SAVE
01134  0084F1  68                    pla
01135  0084F2  8D 0C 7E              sta     RAM_P_SAVE
01136  0084F5  68                    pla
01137  0084F6  8D 06 7E              sta     RAM_PC_SAVE
01138  0084F9  68                    pla
01139  0084FA  8D 07 7E              STA     RAM_PC_SAVE+1
01140  
01141          ; We were in 6502 mode, so save 0 to the bank registers and
01142          ; the high bytes of the 16-bit registers.
01143  0084FD  9C 0E 7E              stz     RAM_PB_SAVE
01144  008500  9C 0F 7E              stz     RAM_DB_SAVE
01145  008503  9C 08 7E              stz     RAM_DP_SAVE
01146  008506  9C 09 7E              stz     RAM_DP_SAVE+1
01147  008509  9C 01 7E              stz     RAM_A_SAVE+1
01148  00850C  9C 03 7E              stz     RAM_X_SAVE+1
01149  00850F  9C 05 7E              STZ     RAM_Y_SAVE+1
01150  
01151          ; Save the LSB (8-bits) of the stack to work-RAM.
01152  008512  BA                    tsx
01153  008513  8E 0A 7E              STX     RAM_SP_SAVE
01154  
01155          ; We know we're in emulation mode, so save "1" to the high-byte
01156          ; of the stack pointer and the E(mulation) flag save area.
01157  008516  A9 01                 lda     #$01
01158  008518  8D 0B 7E              sta     RAM_SP_SAVE+1
01159  00851B  8D 0D 7E              STA     RAM_E_SAVE
01160  
01161          ; Per the comments above, I don't think this is ever actually
01162          ; called from here. Another reason is that the subroutine expects
01163          ; the CPU to be in emulation mode, and if this code were to be
01164          ; executed, it would be in we're in native mode now.
01165  00851E  4C A5 85              JMP     Send_Enter_Reason_and_Sync_With_Debugger
01166  
01167  .enter_native_mode:
01168          ; Switch to native mode.
01169  008521  18                    CLC
01170  008522  FB                    XCE
01171  
01172          ; Set XY and A to 8-bit mode.
01173  008523  E2 30                 SEP     #$30
01174  
01175          ; Save the reason we're entering the monitor into work-RAM.
01176  008525  8F 13 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_ENTER_MONITOR_REASON
01177  
01178          ; We were previously in emulation mode, so indicate this.
01179  008529  A9 01                 LDA     #$1
01180  00852B  8F 0D 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_E_SAVE
01181  
01182          ; Save the CPU context and enter the ROM monitor.
01183  00852F  4C 60 85              JMP     Save_Context_Enter_Monitor
01184  
01185  ; Unless the user overrides the default vector, then this is called
01186  ; when a BRK instruction is executed while in 816 native mode.
01187  BRK_816_Entry_Vector_Default:
01188          ; Set the A register to 8-bit mode and push the low part of it.
01189  008532  E2 20                 SEP     #$20
01190  008534  48                    PHA
01191  
01192          ; We're now running monitor code.
01193  008535  A9 01                 lda     #$01
01194  008537  8F 11 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_IN_MONITOR
01195  
01196          ; Set RAM_ENTER_MONITOR_REASON to 2, indicating a BRK was executed.
01197  00853B  A9 02                 lda     #$02
01198  00853D  80 15                 BRA     Save_Context_Enter_Monitor_816_Mode_With_Reason
01199  
01200  ; Unless the user overrides the default vector, then this is called
01201  ; upon an NMIA while the CPU is in 816 native mode.
01202  NMI_816_Entry_Vector_Default:
01203          ; Set the A register to 8-bit mode and push the low part of it.
01204  00853F  E2 20                 SEP     #$20
01205  008541  48                    PHA
01206  
01207          ; See if we were running monitor code when the NMI ocurred.
01208  008542  AF 11 7E 00           LDA     \3RAM_IN_MONITOR
01209  008546  D0 0A                 BNE     .was_running_monitor_code
01210  
01211          ; We're now running monitor code.
01212  008548  A9 01                 lda     #$01
01213  00854A  8F 11 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_IN_MONITOR
01214  
01215          ; Set RAM_ENTER_MONITOR_REASON to 7, indicating an NMI was generated.
01216  00854E  A9 07                 lda     #$07
01217  008550  80 02                 BRA     Save_Context_Enter_Monitor_816_Mode_With_Reason
01218  
01219  .was_running_monitor_code:
01220          ; An NMI ocurred while running the monitor code. Ignore it by
01221          ; restoring the context and returning from the interrupt.
01222  008552  68                    pla
01223  008553  40                    rti
01224  
01225  ; Called while in 816 native mode to save the CPU context and
01226  ; then enter the ROM monitor.
01227  Save_Context_Enter_Monitor_816_Mode_With_Reason:
01228  008554  E2 20                 SEP     #$20    ; Set the A register to 8-bit mode.
01229  
01230          ; Save the reason we're entering the monitor into work-RAM.
01231  008556  8F 13 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_ENTER_MONITOR_REASON
01232  
01233          ; We were previously in 816 native mode, so indicate this.
01234  00855A  A9 00                 lda     #$00
01235  00855C  8F 0D 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_E_SAVE
01236  
01237  ; Saves the CPU context and enters the ROM monitor, syncing with the debugger.
01238  ; This code is ultimately used by the BRK and NMI handlers in both native and
01239  ; emulation mode (after switching to native mode).
01240  ;
01241  ; Upon entry, the CPU must be in native 816 mode, with A set to 8-bit mode,
01242  ; with the low 8-bits of A already pushed to the stack.
01243  Save_Context_Enter_Monitor:
01244          ; Save the LSB of A into work-RAM.
01245  008560  68                    PLA
01246  008561  8F 00 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_A_SAVE
01247  
01248          ; Save the MSB of A into work-RAM.
01249  008565  EB                    XBA
01250  008566  8F 01 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_A_SAVE+1
01251  
01252          ; Save the data bank into work-RAM.
01253  00856A  8B                    PHB
01254  00856B  68                    pla
01255  00856C  8F 0F 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_DB_SAVE
01256  
01257          ; Switch to data bank 0.
01258  008570  A9 00                 lda     #$00
01259  008572  48                    pha
01260  008573  AB                    PLB
01261  
01262          ; Save 0 into the program bank save area in work-RAM. This value will
01263          ; remain if the CPU was in emulation mode, but it will be overwritten
01264          ; with the correct value later if the CPU was in native mode.
01265  008574  8F 0E 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_PB_SAVE
01266  
01267          ; Save the CPU status register to the area in work-RAM.
01268  008578  68                    pla
01269  008579  8F 0C 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_P_SAVE
01270  
01271          ; Set 16-bit A and XY registers.
01272  00857D  C2 30                 REP     #$30
01273  
01274          ; Save the direct-page register to the save area in work-RAM.
01275  00857F  7B                    TDC
01276  008580  8F 08 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_DP_SAVE
01277  
01278          ; Set the direct-page register to page 0.
01279  008584  A9 00 00              lda     \2#$00
01280  008587  5B                    TCD
01281  
01282          ; Save the X and Y registers (all 16-bits each) to work-RAM.
01283  008588  8E 02 7E              stx     RAM_X_SAVE
01284  00858B  8C 04 7E              STY     RAM_Y_SAVE
01285  
01286          ; Pull the 16-bit PC and save it to work RAM.
01287  00858E  68                    pla
01288  00858F  8D 06 7E              STA     RAM_PC_SAVE
01289  
01290          ; Set A to 8-bit mode.
01291  008592  E2 20                 SEP     #$20
01292  
01293          ; See if the CPU was in '02 '816 mode when it was interrupted.
01294  008594  AD 0D 7E              LDA     RAM_E_SAVE
01295  008597  D0 04                 BNE     .was_in_emulation_mode
01296  
01297          ; The CPU was in native mode. Pull the program bank and save it.
01298  008599  68                    pla
01299  00859A  8D 0E 7E              STA     RAM_PB_SAVE
01300  
01301  .was_in_emulation_mode:
01302          ; Save all 16-bits of the stack pointer. If the CPU was in emulation
01303          ; mode, the MSB will be saved as "1".
01304  00859D  BA                    tsx
01305  00859E  8E 0A 7E              STX     RAM_SP_SAVE
01306  
01307          ; Set 8-bit XY registers. At this point, A and XY are both 8-bit.
01308  0085A1  E2 10                 SEP     #$10
01309  
01310          ; The user's CPU context is now fully saved into work-RAM. Switch
01311          ; back into emulation mode.
01312  0085A3  38                    SEC
01313  0085A4  FB                    XCE
01314  
01315  ; Sends the reason the monitor (debugger) was entered, and then syncs
01316  ; with the debugger, allowing the debugger to control the device.
01317  Send_Enter_Reason_and_Sync_With_Debugger:
01318  
01319          ; Save the state of the system VIA's PCR so it can be restored later.
01320  0085A5  20 64 86              JSR     Save_VIA_PCR_State
01321  
01322          ; Send the reason we entered the monitor to the debugger.
01323  0085A8  AD 13 7E              LDA     RAM_ENTER_MONITOR_REASON
01324  0085AB  20 2B 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
01325  
01326          ; Save the first five zero-page values, and sync with debugger.
01327  0085AE  4C DB 81              JMP     Save_ZP_Sync_With_Debugger
01328  
01329  ; Called in emulation mode upon system reset.
01330  ; Initializes the system VIA (the USB debugger), and syncs with the USB chip.
01331  Initialize_System_VIA:
01332  
01333          ; Disable PB7, shift register, timer T1 interrupt.
01334  0085B1  A9 00                 lda     #$00
01335  0085B3  8D EB 7F              STA     SYSTEM_VIA_ACR
01336  
01337          ; Cx1/Cx2 as inputs with negative active edge, for both ports. These
01338          ; aren't used for the system VIA debugging interface, but the Cx2
01339          ; lines are connected to the FLASH, and they select the bank. Setting
01340          ; them as inputs allows the pullups to automatically select the bank
01341          ; which contains the factory-programmed FLASH bank with the monitor.
01342  0085B6  A9 00                 lda     #$00
01343  0085B8  8D EC 7F              STA     SYSTEM_VIA_PCR
01344  
01345          ; Save the PCR in work-RAM so it can be restored later.
01346  0085BB  8D 1C 7E              STA     RAM_PCR_SAVE
01347  
01348          ; Preset port B output for $18 (TUSB_RDB and PB4-not-connected high).
01349  0085BE  A9 18                 lda     #$18
01350  0085C0  8D E0 7F              STA     SYSTEM_VIA_IOB
01351  
01352          ; Set PB2 (TUSB_WR), PB3 (TUSB_RDB), and PB4 (N.C.) as outputs. This
01353          ; has the effect of writing $FF to the USB FIFO when the RESET button
01354          ; is pressed. When RESET is pressed, it causes the system VIA to output
01355          ; high on TUSB_WR, then when this write sets TUSB_WR low, the high-to-
01356          ; low transition on TUSB_WR triggers a write to the USB FIFO. At this
01357          ; point, port A (the USB FIFO data lines) are not being driven, and
01358          ; either float high, or are pulled high internally, because this
01359          ; triggers a write of $FF to the USB FIFO.
01360  0085C3  A9 1C                 lda     #$1C
01361  0085C5  8D E2 7F              STA     SYSTEM_VIA_DDRB
01362  
01363          ; Save DDRB in work-RAM. Not sure why, since it is never used again.
01364  0085C8  8D 1D 7E              STA     RAM_DDRB_SAVE
01365  
01366          ; Set all IO on port A to inputs.
01367  0085CB  A9 00                 LDA     #$00
01368  0085CD  8D E3 7F              STA     SYSTEM_VIA_DDRA
01369  
01370          ; Save DDRA in work-RAM. Not sure why, since it is never used again.
01371  0085D0  8D 1E 7E              STA     RAM_DDRA_SAVE
01372  
01373          ; Read port B (USB status and control lines) and save it on the stack.
01374  0085D3  AD E0 7F              lda     SYSTEM_VIA_IOB
01375  0085D6  48                    PHA
01376  
01377          ; Mask out bit 4, which is not connected.
01378  0085D7  29 EF                 AND     #$EF
01379  
01380          ; Write the result back. Not sure why since only bit 4 changes, and
01381          ; it is not connected (according to schematic rev. C, Dec. 15, 2020).
01382  0085D9  8D E0 7F              STA     SYSTEM_VIA_IOB
01383  
01384          ; Delay for $5D*256 loop cycles.
01385  0085DC  A2 5D                 LDX     #$5D
01386  0085DE  20 59 86              JSR     Delay_Loop
01387  
01388          ; Pull the original port B value, and write it back to the port.
01389  0085E1  68                    PLA
01390  0085E2  8D E0 7F              STA     SYSTEM_VIA_IOB
01391  
01392          ; Wait until PB5 (TUSB_PWRENB) goes low, indicating it's powered up.
01393  0085E5  A9 20                 lda     #$20
01394  0085E7  2C E0 7F      .loop:  bit     SYSTEM_VIA_IOB
01395  0085EA  D0 FB                 BNE     .loop
01396  
01397          ; If PB6 (not connected) is 0, then make a no-op call. Why?!?
01398  0085EC  AD E0 7F              LDA     SYSTEM_VIA_IOB
01399  0085EF  29 40                 and     #$40
01400  0085F1  F0 65                 BEQ     Do_Nothing_Subroutine_1
01401  
01402          ; All done.
01403  0085F3  60                    RTS
01404  
01405  ; Returns 1 in A if there is data available to be read, 0 if not.
01406  Is_VIA_USB_RX_Data_Avail:
01407  
01408          ; Set all bits on port A to inputs.
01409  0085F4  A9 00                 LDA     #$00
01410  0085F6  8D E3 7F              STA     SYSTEM_VIA_DDRA
01411  
01412          ; See if PB1 (TUSB_RXFB) is high.
01413  0085F9  A9 02                 LDA     #$02
01414  0085FB  2C E0 7F              bit     SYSTEM_VIA_IOB
01415  0085FE  D0 03                 bne     .not_zero
01416  
01417          ; It is low, meaning there is data available to read.
01418  008600  A9 01                 LDA     #$01
01419  008602  60                    RTS
01420  
01421  .not_zero:
01422          ; It is high, meaning there is no data available to read.
01423  008603  A9 00                 LDA     #$00
01424  008605  60                    RTS
01425  
01426  ; Waits for a byte to be ready on the USB FIFO and then reads it, returning
01427  ; the value read in the A register.
01428  Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX:
01429          ; Set all bits on port A to inputs.
01430  008606  A9 00                 lda     #$00
01431  008608  8D E3 7F              STA     SYSTEM_VIA_DDRA
01432  
01433          ; Set up to test PB1 (TUSB_RXFB).
01434  00860B  A9 02                 LDA     #$02
01435  
01436          ; Wait for PB1 (TUSB_RXFB) to be low. This indicates data can be
01437          ; read from the FIFO by strobing PB3 low then high again.
01438  .wait_for_rxfb_low:
01439  00860D  2C E0 7F              bit     SYSTEM_VIA_IOB
01440  008610  D0 FB                 BNE     .wait_for_rxfb_low
01441  
01442          ; Perform a read-modify-write on port B, clearing PB3 (TUSB_RDB).
01443          ; This triggers the FIFO to drive the received byte on port A.
01444  008612  AD E0 7F              lda     SYSTEM_VIA_IOB
01445  008615  09 08                 ora     #$08    ; Save a copy of port B with PB3 set high.
01446  008617  AA                    tax     ; This will be used later.
01447  008618  29 F7                 and     #$F7
01448  00861A  8D E0 7F              STA     SYSTEM_VIA_IOB
01449  
01450          ; Wait for the FIFO to drive the data and the lines to settle
01451          ; (between 20ns and 50ns, according to the datasheet).
01452  00861D  EA                    nop
01453  00861E  EA                    nop
01454  00861F  EA                    nop
01455  008620  EA                    NOP
01456  
01457          ; Read the data byte from the FIFO on port A.
01458  008621  AD E1 7F              LDA     SYSTEM_VIA_IOA
01459  
01460          ; Restore the original value of port B, while setting PB3 high again.
01461  008624  8E E0 7F              stx     SYSTEM_VIA_IOB
01462  
01463          ; We're done. The byte read is in A.
01464  008627  60                    RTS
01465  
01466          ; Apparently unused code.
01467  008628  A9 EE                 lda     #$EE
01468  00862A  60                    rts
01469  
01470  ; Sends the byte stored in A to the debugger, waiting until it can be sent.
01471  Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX:
01472  
01473          ; Set all bits on port A to inputs.
01474  00862B  A2 00                 ldx     #$00
01475  00862D  8E E3 7F              STX     SYSTEM_VIA_DDRA
01476  
01477          ; Write register A to port A. This has no effect on the actual
01478          ; output pin until port A is set as an output.
01479  008630  8D E1 7F              STA     SYSTEM_VIA_IOA
01480  
01481          ; Set up register A to test port B, bit 0 (TUSB_TXEB).
01482  008633  A9 01                 LDA     #$01
01483  
01484          ; Wait for PB0 (TUSB_TXEB) to be low. This indicates data can be
01485          ; written to the FIFO by strobing PB2 (TUSB_WR) high then low.
01486  .wait_for_txeb_low:
01487  008635  2C E0 7F              bit     SYSTEM_VIA_IOB
01488  008638  D0 FB                 BNE     .wait_for_txeb_low
01489  
01490          ; Perform a read-modify-write on port B, setting bit 2 (TUSB_WR).
01491          ; Save the original value in X temporarily.
01492  00863A  AD E0 7F              lda     SYSTEM_VIA_IOB
01493  00863D  29 FB                 AND     #$FB	; Save a copy of port B with PB2 low.
01494  00863F  AA                    TAX
01495  008640  09 04                 ora     #$04	; Set PB2 high.
01496  008642  8D E0 7F              STA     SYSTEM_VIA_IOB
01497  
01498          ; Set all bits on port A to outputs. This causes the pin outputs
01499          ; to be set to what we wrote to port A earlier in the subroutine.
01500  008645  A9 FF                 lda     #$FF
01501  008647  8D E3 7F              STA     SYSTEM_VIA_DDRA
01502  
01503          ; Wait for the port A outputs to settle. The datasheet says this
01504          ; must be held at least 20 ns before PB2 (TUSB_WR) is brought low.
01505  00864A  EA                    NOP
01506  00864B  EA                    NOP
01507  
01508          ; Write the original port B value back, setting PB2 back to low.
01509  00864C  8E E0 7F              STX     SYSTEM_VIA_IOB
01510  
01511          ; Read port A. But why? The values read should be the actual
01512          ; values driven on the pins, which may not be what we commanded
01513          ; them to if, for example, they are heavily loaded. This value
01514          ; is returned in the A register, and could be examined by the
01515          ; caller. But this is not used anywhere in the monitor.
01516  00864F  AD E1 7F              LDA     SYSTEM_VIA_IOA
01517  
01518          ; Set all bits in port A as inputs.
01519  008652  A2 00                 ldx     #$00
01520  008654  8E E3 7F              STX     SYSTEM_VIA_DDRA
01521  
01522          ; All done.
01523  008657  60                    rts
01524  
01525  ; A subroutine which does absolutely nothing.
01526  Do_Nothing_Subroutine_1:
01527  008658  60                    rts
01528  
01529  ; Delays by looping 256*X times.
01530  Delay_Loop:
01531  008659  DA                    phx
01532  00865A  A2 00                 ldx     #$00
01533  .loop_256_times:
01534  00865C  CA                    dex
01535  00865D  D0 FD                 bne     .loop_256_times
01536  00865F  FA                    plx
01537  008660  CA                    dex
01538  008661  D0 F6                 bne     Delay_Loop
01539  008663  60                    rts
01540  
01541  ; Saves the current VIA PCR state into work-RAM. This is done after running
01542  ; user code, and before modifying PCR once returning to the monitor. This is
01543  ; necessary in case the user modifies PCR, for example, to control the active
01544  ; banks on the FLASH.
01545  Save_VIA_PCR_State:
01546  008664  AD EC 7F              lda     SYSTEM_VIA_PCR
01547  008667  8D 1C 7E              sta     RAM_PCR_SAVE
01548  00866A  60                    rts
01549  
01550  ; Restores the state of the system VIA's PCR register to what it was when
01551  ; the monitor interrupted the user's code.
01552  Restore_VIA_PCR_State:
01553  00866B  AD 1C 7E              lda     RAM_PCR_SAVE
01554  00866E  8D EC 7F              sta     SYSTEM_VIA_PCR
01555  008671  60                    rts
01556  
01557  ; The second subroutine which does absolutely nothing.
01558  Do_Nothing_Subroutine_2:
01559  008672  60                    rts
01560  
01561  ; The third subroutine which does absolutely nothing.
01562  Do_Nothing_Subroutine_3:
01563  008673  60                    rts
01564  008674  60                    rts
01565  008675  60                    rts
01566  008676  60                    RTS
01567
